<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d1ba85e7-3127-4a17-a5e0-a63525fd4801'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText13904571975113965916" style="display:none"><i>I see him and I know what this turmoil inside of me means: He's the one. My forever.</i><br /><br />Kayla is the nature lover, the all-American beauty who can't understand why she's so drawn to distant, brooding Lucas. Adopted as a young child, she has no way of knowing that she's inherited a terrifying-and thrilling-gene that will change her life forever.<br /><br />Lucas is dangerous, gorgeous... and a werewolf. As leader of the Dark Guardians, shape-shifters who gather deep within the state park, he has sworn to protect his pack. But when Lucas finds his true soul mate, his love could put them all in harm's way.<br /><br />As Lucas and Kayla struggle with their feelings for each other, a greater danger lurks: Humans have discovered the Dark Guardians and are planning their destruction. Kayla must choose between the life she knows and the love she feels certain is her destiny.</span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_9914850').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_9914850').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer875586837" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13824177533068429251"><b>
  <i>I see him and I know what this turmoil inside of me means: He's the one. My forever. </i>
</b><br/><br/>Fucking great, so you know you want to spend the rest of your life with a dude whom you had barely talked to/interacted with before when you're at the tender age of seventeen?<br/><br/>Not to mention, this twenty-something dude (or was he supposed to be 19?) had been eyeing the heroine and thinking about making her his mate back when she was sixteen years old.<br/><br/>I need to calm the fuck down.<br/><br/><i>Moonlight</i> is a dull, <i>extremely</i></span>
  <span id="freeText13824177533068429251" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>I see him and I know what this turmoil inside of me means: He's the one. My forever. </i>
</b><br /><br />Fucking great, so you know you want to spend the rest of your life with a dude whom you had barely talked to/interacted with before when you're at the tender age of seventeen?<br /><br />Not to mention, this twenty-something dude (or was he supposed to be 19?) had been eyeing the heroine and thinking about making her his mate back when she was sixteen years old.<br /><br />I need to calm the fuck down.<br /><br /><i>Moonlight</i> is a dull, <i>extremely</i> unoriginal Twilight rip-off which isn't even worthy of a proper review, the only difference between this book and Twilight is that this time around the sexy hot brooding guy is the werewolf.<br /><br />Did I mention that the gender roles and love relationships in the book is Dark Age level of backward as well? It's as though sex revolution and feminism never happens.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13824177533068429251" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=pure-awesomeness">pure-awesomeness</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer213117542" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7110043608278287794"><b>Rating:</b> 4.5 stars<br/><br/>Ever get that giggly feeling in your stomach when you read a really, <i>really</i> cute book? That's what I got from reading <b>Moonlight</b>. I love this book with all my heart! <br/><br/>Werewolf (or shape-shifter) books are easy to find nowadays, but there are only few that actually pull you into the story and refuse to let go — for me, <b>Moonlight</b> was one of them! The synopsis doesn't do this book justice because I started it with a hesitant mind and ended up loving it. <br/><br/>I can't ask for a more perfect</span>
  <span id="freeText7110043608278287794" style="display:none"><b>Rating:</b> 4.5 stars<br /><br />Ever get that giggly feeling in your stomach when you read a really, <i>really</i> cute book? That's what I got from reading <b>Moonlight</b>. I love this book with all my heart! <br /><br />Werewolf (or shape-shifter) books are easy to find nowadays, but there are only few that actually pull you into the story and refuse to let go — for me, <b>Moonlight</b> was one of them! The synopsis doesn't do this book justice because I started it with a hesitant mind and ended up loving it. <br /><br />I can't ask for a more perfect voice for this novel! Kayla is such a sweet, nature-loving character who I adored from page one. And Lucas is the leader of the Dark Guardians who made me sigh every time he was around. There's nothing hotter than a bad-ass shape-shifter, and there's nothing sweeter than Kayla and Lucas's relationship! <br /><br />The plot, although admittedly a little predictable, is always fun to read because of the awesome way it's written and the fast-paced plot. <b>Moonlight</b> is so much lighter and more enjoyable than I ever could've imagined, and I would recommend it to everyone without a doubt! :) <br /><br /><b>BUY or BORROW?:</b> This is the kind of book I wish I had on my shelf, because the first thing I want to do is go back and read it again! It's all the sweetness and fun without being cheesy!<br /><br />(Original review at <a href="http://diminutivemimi.blogspot.com/2011/09/review-moonlight.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Mimi Valentine's YA Review Blog</a>)</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nozomi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nozomi" href="/user/show/1988380-nozomi">Nozomi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Nozomi by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/1909179-shannon-twilight-sleep">Shannon (Twilight Sleep)</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1988380-nozomi?shelf=werewolf">werewolf</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer53424751" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2134010730056829359">Well, let's jump on the <u>Twilight</u> bandwagon, shall we? Except, this time, we'll do it with werewolves.<br/><br/>This book is overall okay, but I'm going to be cruel and use it as an example of why I previously avoided most YA in the first place. It was unsatisfying and extremely predictable. The characters were not well developed, and there was a backstory that I felt could have been included, or at least more described. Hawthorne's characters fluctuated from sounding too young to using words that I felt a</span>
  <span id="freeText2134010730056829359" style="display:none">Well, let's jump on the <u>Twilight</u> bandwagon, shall we? Except, this time, we'll do it with werewolves.<br /><br />This book is overall okay, but I'm going to be cruel and use it as an example of why I previously avoided most YA in the first place. It was unsatisfying and extremely predictable. The characters were not well developed, and there was a backstory that I felt could have been included, or at least more described. Hawthorne's characters fluctuated from sounding too young to using words that I felt an average seventeen-year-old wouldn't know yet.<br /><br />I'm going to say something I'm probably going to regret, but Stephenie Meyer was at least original. The werewolf "imprinting" plotline in her series was clearly imitated in this book. The male werewolves in this book also decide on a soul mate on the basis of "love at first sight." Then they go and get a tattoo of their beloved's name somewhere on their backs. Can you say ridiculous and the most unadvised thing to do in real life? Can you also see the sexism in male and female roles?<br /><br />The werewolves here also communicate by telepathy, but I think that's more common.<br /><br />Not to mention the book cover is embarrassing, but the author has nothing to do with that.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2134010730056829359" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2545195-kay?shelf=when-i-said-ya-i-did-not-mean-this">when-i-said-ya-i-did-not-mean-this</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer89920614" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1839431439257265565">There was just something... wrong with this book. There was nothing particularly bad about the writing, or even the plot - but there was just something about it that made it a rather uneventful read. But what exactly?<br/><br/>When I finished it - which took a while despite being a ludicrously easy read - I finally worked out what it was: it was a Middle Grade novel with a Young Adult plot.<br/><br/>The writing was just slightly too simple, the cover-ups too obvious, and the emotions underdeveloped. While this is u</span>
  <span id="freeText1839431439257265565" style="display:none">There was just something... wrong with this book. There was nothing particularly bad about the writing, or even the plot - but there was just something about it that made it a rather uneventful read. But what exactly?<br /><br />When I finished it - which took a while despite being a ludicrously easy read - I finally worked out what it was: it was a Middle Grade novel with a Young Adult plot.<br /><br />The writing was just slightly too simple, the cover-ups too obvious, and the emotions underdeveloped. While this is understandable when your narrator is 12 - it is harder when she is a teen. And when the plot involves werewolves and undying love, there is a certain amount of maturity that you expect from the writing and the characters.<br /><br />Bottom line? Skip it - even if you are a die-hard YA Romance lover. I don't plan on getting the next books - life is too short to read books you a apathetic about.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://deadbookdarling.blogspot.com/2010/01/review-moonlight-dark-guardian-book-1.html">http://deadbookdarling.blogspot.com/2...</a></span>

<div id="review_86537605" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/86537605" />
    <a title="Shera (Book Whispers)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3167178-shera-book-whispers"><img alt="Shera (Book Whispers)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1446841556p2/3167178.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/86537605?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shera (Book Whispers)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shera (Book Whispers)" href="/user/show/3167178-shera-book-whispers">Shera (Book Whispers)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3167178-shera-book-whispers?shelf=ya-paranormal-uf">ya-paranormal-uf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3167178-shera-book-whispers?shelf=werewolves">werewolves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3167178-shera-book-whispers?shelf=2009">2009</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer86537605" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18148860204824720058"><b>Genre:</b> Paranormal YA (UF) <br/><br/>Moonlight is a guilty pleasure. Not because it has naughty sex scenes or bad language jumping off the page—quite the opposite. It's pretty sweet and innocent, like PNR novels accept YA approved. Of course I have to say right up front if you’re seeking something that has mind blowing writing, hidden depths, and a unique plot this is the not the book. It’s not really fantastic in any form, but there is something about it that draws a reader in and just takes hold.<br/><br/>Moonligh</span>
  <span id="freeText18148860204824720058" style="display:none"><b>Genre:</b> Paranormal YA (UF) <br /><br />Moonlight is a guilty pleasure. Not because it has naughty sex scenes or bad language jumping off the page—quite the opposite. It's pretty sweet and innocent, like PNR novels accept YA approved. Of course I have to say right up front if you’re seeking something that has mind blowing writing, hidden depths, and a unique plot this is the not the book. It’s not really fantastic in any form, but there is something about it that draws a reader in and just takes hold.<br /><br />Moonlight goes where you expect it to and with a 263 page count it really doesn't get to explore all the fantastic ideas that are lurking around. It focuses on girl meets wolf boy, girl is soon to turn wolf, wolf boy perfects girl, and they mate for life. Moonlight is not all romance, there is an interesting plot about humans trying to get the secrets of the Guardians (werewolves) and an evil brother bent on revenge. <br /><br />Again for how small it is, the characters are well fleshed out. This is Kayla’s journey to grow up and become her “true-self”. Lucas is the cliché brooding male lead that the ladies love to swoon over; mysterious, quiet, and devoted to his future woman. Kayla and Lucas bonded well together, both being really likable.<br /><br />The world of the Guardians is clearly something that needs to be explored more in later books, there are more boys and girls to turn into wolves and find mates. All of the guys already have their future mates tattooed onto them, so my curiosity is killing me to see if I guessed the right couples. In the short course of the book Hawthorne made me appreciate the cast of side characters. <br /><br />While it reads like a beach book, it does not have the tone of one. It deals with death, loss, fear, and dealing with the choices we make and living with them. There’s not much meat to it, but readers will find themselves engrossed in the world of the Guardians and the mystery of finding a life mate. Moonlight’s power is to take an “adult” plot from paranormal romances and turn it in to a YA read. <br /><br /><b>Sexual Content:</b><br />Kissing and a few heavy make out scenes. There is a scene where a boy pushes himself on to the main character in the acts of making it look like he might rape her. A few dirty jokes and questions sprinkled in every now and again.<br /><br /><b>3/5- Adored it, just a few minor details held it back</b> <br /><br /><i>
  <b>Originally posted at <a href="http://shera-bookwhispers.blogspot.com/2011/03/review-moonlight-by-rachel-hawthorne.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Whispers</a>.</b>
</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="18148860204824720058" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1296353925" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1296353925" />
    <a title="Carrie (The Butterfly Reader)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30055062-carrie-the-butterfly-reader"><img alt="Carrie (The Butterfly Reader)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594582527p2/30055062.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer4432216030177317825">For more of my reviews, check out my blog: <a href='http://www.sweetcherry69.blogspot.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Book Goddess</a><br/><br/><br/>I loved the premise of this book, the world. The idea was so amazing. But it fell flat. I wanted to love this book so freaking much but I couldn't. It was rather boring and strange. Kayla is in love with a boy who never speaks to her. He is the cliche bad boy. He is brooding and mysterious. Until you get to know him, then he becomes a mushy and reminds me of a puppy.<br/><br/>The plot goes like this. Kayla lost her family at a young age, she was a</span>
  <span id="freeText4432216030177317825" style="display:none">For more of my reviews, check out my blog: <a href="http://www.sweetcherry69.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">The Book Goddess</a><br /><br /><br />I loved the premise of this book, the world. The idea was so amazing. But it fell flat. I wanted to love this book so freaking much but I couldn't. It was rather boring and strange. Kayla is in love with a boy who never speaks to her. He is the cliche bad boy. He is brooding and mysterious. Until you get to know him, then he becomes a mushy and reminds me of a puppy.<br /><br />The plot goes like this. Kayla lost her family at a young age, she was adopted by a loving couple who takes her camping in the forest where her family was killed. A year later she goes back and is now what we call a guide. She meets all these shifters, but doesn't know they are shifters and that she is one of them too. The bad guys are trying to catch a werewolf and Lucus has family issues with his brother who tells the bad guys about them being shifters. The bad guys end up getting away and Lucus kills his brother. Kayla finds out she is Lucus's mate and ends up deciding to be with him. It's all quite childish, their love.<br /><br />I hate intsa love and that's what this book has. The writing was plain and simplistic. Nothing special. The idea was awesome but so poorly flushed out. It just breaks my heart because I wanted to write this book but from now on, I'm going to stay away from this author. I've not liked anything she's written.<br /></span>

  <span id="freeText14841360394551122430" style="display:none">This book was a disappointment. The dialogue was off and seemed scripted. Wasn't natural. I don't see what's the deal with the Dark Guardians. Shouldn't all werewolves or "shifters" hold their secrets and guard the others from evil and harm? All it takes is for her to swear? When I could tell that Hawthorne didn't mean to put an ending to the human scientists in this book, though it was a problem that needed solving, it felt like Hawthorne just completely forgot about them and cut off their part in this book. The villain that did die in this book seemed like the real bad guy. I would have rather liked him to stay.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15660640300135292652">Moonlight follows Kayla, a girl working as a Sherpa (guide) in a dense national forest for the summer. She had visited the forest the summer before because her therapist said she needed to find closure. Basically, when she was little her parents were killed in the forest and she has never gotten over it (rightly so). Yet she is drawn to the forest and the handsome Sherpa leader Lucas. All is not as it seems in this book filled with a group of crazy scientists, forest adventures, and werewolves (</span>
  <span id="freeText15660640300135292652" style="display:none">Moonlight follows Kayla, a girl working as a Sherpa (guide) in a dense national forest for the summer. She had visited the forest the summer before because her therapist said she needed to find closure. Basically, when she was little her parents were killed in the forest and she has never gotten over it (rightly so). Yet she is drawn to the forest and the handsome Sherpa leader Lucas. All is not as it seems in this book filled with a group of crazy scientists, forest adventures, and werewolves (you heard me right). Kayla Madison is excited about spending the summer as a sherpa in the dense national forest. <br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1570289003ra/28248815.gif" width="360" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That sums up my feelings for this book pretty well. I mean I went into it expecting the teen angst werewolf story (I've been needing all the books I read when I was a teen recently). However, maybe because I have been reading a lot of stories like this recently, but his one was just okay. The story just seemed a bit too fast paced for me. The relationship went from 0 to 100 immediately. I felt like maybe I was missing 100 pages or something. IDK, not my favorite, but it wasn't bad or anything. It just lacked the depth I wanted. Will I read it again in 10 years when I want to relive my werewolf fangirl days once again? Yeah, probably. <br><br></span>

<div id="review_96232498" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/96232498" />
    <a title="Katelyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3264162-katelyn"><img alt="Katelyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1276722168p2/3264162.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/96232498?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katelyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katelyn" href="/user/show/3264162-katelyn">Katelyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3264162-katelyn?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer96232498" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7427634973798628347">I can't remember how I came upon this series, but what I do know is that I'm so glad I did! Moonlight is the first in the Dark Guardian series and once again I've found myself a new series that I already can't get enough of.<br/><br/>As a fan of the paranormal genre, I'm always excited when I find a book within that genre that has a new twist to the old storyline. The Dark Guardians' series has taken the old tales of werewolves and produced a new and unique spin on the characters.<br/><br/>Rachel Hawthorne created </span>
  <span id="freeText7427634973798628347" style="display:none">I can't remember how I came upon this series, but what I do know is that I'm so glad I did! Moonlight is the first in the Dark Guardian series and once again I've found myself a new series that I already can't get enough of.<br /><br />As a fan of the paranormal genre, I'm always excited when I find a book within that genre that has a new twist to the old storyline. The Dark Guardians' series has taken the old tales of werewolves and produced a new and unique spin on the characters.<br /><br />Rachel Hawthorne created a story out of her very realistic world and had me believing instantly! Her main characters, Kayla and Lucas were great. Brave and compelling Kayla meshed very well with the dark and brooding Lucas. Their story was romantic, yet frustrating, moving and yet so much fun. I loved it all!<br /><br />With werewolves being a reality and some ill intent humans after them for their own nefarious purposes, readers will be on edge to see if Kayla and Lucas will be able to defeat them and remain safe or if their in deeper water than they thought. Will their romance and feelings be enough to keep them strong for the fight ahead, or will it all be just too much for Kayla to handle with the other revelations she's faced with?<br /><br />I've always been a fast reader but I was able to really fly through this book, it took only one day for me to finish and after I was done I wanted to jump right into the next installment. There's a little bit of everything in this series; romance, adventure, action and suspense, plenty of description and depth to keep you interested and wanting to come back for more. I really had fun with this one and already ordered the second installment, Full Moon, because I just can't stand not knowing what will happen next, I'm hooked yet again! I'm really looking forward to see where Hawthorne and her Dark Guardians' series takes me next!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7427634973798628347" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/104823-kate?shelf=2009">2009</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/104823-kate?shelf=age-ya">age-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/104823-kate?shelf=werewolves">werewolves</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer65647016" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3741683776996856782">I read this in one day... it was definitely a quick read although helped by the fact that I had about an hour sitting by myself at Barnes & Noble waiting for my friend Melissa to arrive for the Carrie Jones signing (she was cool and I got my copy and my library's copy of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4070493.Need' title='Need by Carrie Jones' rel='nofollow noopener'>Need</a> signed - a great werewolf book if you enjoyed <i>Moonlight</i>). <br/><br/>So this was a tiny bit predictable. I kind of wished there wasn't a prologue at the beginning - it was one of those prologues that is actually a scene from the end o</span>
  <span id="freeText3741683776996856782" style="display:none">I read this in one day... it was definitely a quick read although helped by the fact that I had about an hour sitting by myself at Barnes &amp; Noble waiting for my friend Melissa to arrive for the Carrie Jones signing (she was cool and I got my copy and my library's copy of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4070493.Need" title="Need by Carrie Jones" rel="nofollow noopener">Need</a> signed - a great werewolf book if you enjoyed <i>Moonlight</i>). <br /><br />So this was a tiny bit predictable. I kind of wished there wasn't a prologue at the beginning - it was one of those prologues that is actually a scene from the end of the book, and then the whole story leads up to it - because I felt that it gave the whole story away. I mean, you know right from the beginning that there are actually werewolves and the main character Kayla now believes in them. I would have preferred to find out as Kayla did that werewolves were real. Lucas's behavior throughout the story made perfect sense to the reader, who knows that he is a werewolf, and it was kind of frustrating as Kayla blundered around not yet aware of this. I just didn't feel that the prologue added to it at all.<br /><br />However, the chemistry between Kayla and Lucas was good, and I liked the werewolf world that author is building here. I wished there was a little bit more depth and background to the story, since the major climactic point seemed to jump out of nowhere. From the summaries I've read, the next book in the series looks at another of the werewolf pairs, Lindsay and Rafe, so perhaps now that we're all aware of the werewolf community there will be more depth to it in the rest of the series. <i>Moonlight</i> was a fun read, although I doubt I'll be picking up the next one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3741683776996856782" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsey Simard Toutant" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsey Simard Toutant" href="/user/show/3265473-lindsey-simard-toutant">Lindsey Simard Toutant</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer106480917" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6129085696052178805">At 320 pages Moonlight, the first book in the Dark Guardian series, is a quick read but it's packed with romance, suspense, and a new take on shape shifters. This series is definitely geared for young adults and although the majority of books I am currently reading are from the young adult genre I found this book to be a little young for me. <br/><br/><br/>As a protagonist I feel Kayla authentically represents your average teenage girl dealing with complex and unexpected obstacles. Although at times Kayla is p</span>
  <span id="freeText6129085696052178805" style="display:none">At 320 pages Moonlight, the first book in the Dark Guardian series, is a quick read but it's packed with romance, suspense, and a new take on shape shifters. This series is definitely geared for young adults and although the majority of books I am currently reading are from the young adult genre I found this book to be a little young for me. <br /><br /><br />As a protagonist I feel Kayla authentically represents your average teenage girl dealing with complex and unexpected obstacles. Although at times Kayla is portrayed as insecure and vulnerable her personality is balanced with courage and loyalty. I think Lucas caters to that unexplainable attraction young women have to "bad boys" and it feeds the fantasy that maybe that bad boy just needed the right girl to come along. <br /><br /><br />I really enjoyed that the majority of the book takes place in the wilderness. I am an avid camper so the thought that while hiking through the woods there could be a human in wolf form following me sends shivers down my spine! <br /><br /><br />I really love the history of shape shifters that Hawthorne delves into periodically throughout the progression of Moonlight. Additionally she reveals just enough about the supporting characters to excite the reader for the additional Dark Guardian novels. As a reader I love when an author explores other characters within the series and I look forward to reading Dark Guardian three, Full Moon. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6129085696052178805" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText5789335295376998339" style="display:none">When Kayla becomes a wilderness tour guide for the summer the most she expects is to spend a lot of time in the woods and to face her fears. She never expects to find out her friends are Shifters. Or to find her soul-mate.<br /><br />Honestly this book was just okay. It wasn't bad but it wasn't great either. It was fluff. I read it in one sitting.<br />The Characters are a little one dimensional. Lucas was a good character. He was mysterious and intriguing but Kayla was a little on the annoying side. The side characters were introduced nicely. The author did a great job of setting up for the rest of the series.<br />The backstory for the Shifters and the Dark Guardians was well done. It left me wanting to know more about the pack. In my opinion the ending felt a little rushed. The author spent too much time on minor elements of the story when she should have put more into the ending.<br />Regardless of all that I still enjoyed the book. It was a very fast read and I'm looking forward to reading Full Moon. <br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.pureimaginationblog.com/">http://www.pureimaginationblog.com/</a></span>

  <span id="freeText2882636942919300462" style="display:none">This book is good. I expected much from Rachel Hawthorne. As usual, it's well written. BUT..BUT It's just too predictable. Adopted as a young child, she has no way of knowing that she's inherited a terrifying—and thrilling—gene that will change her life forever. <br /><br />lucas is dangerous, gorgeous . . . and a werewolf. As leader of the Dark Guardians, shape-shifters who gather deep within the state park, he has sworn to protect his pack. But when Lucas finds his true soul mate, his love could put them all in harm's way. <br /><br />As Lucas and Kayla struggle with their feelings for each other, a greater danger lurks: Humans have discovered the Dark Guardians and are planning their destruction. Kayla must choose between the life she knows and the love she feels certain is her destiny. <br />--------------------------------------------------------------------<br /><br />I hate this line <b>"kayla is the nature lover, the all-American beauty who can't understand why she's so drawn to distant, brooding Lucas."</b><br />It rankles me that they describe Kayla like that. WHen I read it, I wanted to smirk. <i>Oh, of course the heroine has to be a beauty if not why would the hero fell in love with her.</i> That's the first thing that come into my mind. What a generic half hearted attempt of description.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2882636942919300462" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15027106464125535374">I loved it! I thoroughly enjoyed this book. From the moment I started reading I found it difficult to stop and I ended up reading it in one sitting.   <span id="freeText15027106464125535374" style="display:none">I loved it! I thoroughly enjoyed this book. From the moment I started reading I found it difficult to stop and I ended up reading it in one sitting. It was a quick, fun, easy read. <br />I thought the storyline was excellent and I loved the overall feeling of this book. From the very beginning the story was filled with mystery and I was eager to know just what had happened in Kayla’s past and what would happen to her next. <br />I enjoyed how this book was set outdoors for the most part. It was nice seeing it set in the woods and within nature. <br />I liked the idea of the wolves and while it was a very basic set out, it had enough uniqueness to make it very entertaining. I loved all the characters. Kayla, Lucas, Lindsey, Brittany, Connor and Rafe were all interesting. <br />Kayla was a very basic heroine, but I liked her. She was sweet, but strong enough. The only thing that bothered me.....was that at times I felt she could be very naive. She refused to believe or consider certain things at times, even when the evidence was right before her eyes. <br />Lucas was very sexy, and I loved how much he protected Kayla. <br />I thought it was sooooo cute how their relationship changed. There was the attraction between them, and the fact that they were mates, and yet Lucas didn’t act on it until it was required.<br /><br />I think this was a wonderful book and I look forward to reading the rest of the series. <br /></span>

  <span id="freeText3229540413837890391" style="display:none">I first read this series a few years ago, but it popped into my head the other night and I decided to read it again. It was just as much fun this time around. <br /><br />Kayla's parents were tragically killed in front of her when she was only five. She is now seventeen and trying to face her demons by returning to the woods where her parents were killed. She gets a job at the national forest and helps lead people on hikes through the park. She has made friends with the other “Sherpas” and has a major crush on their boss Lucas. Lucas was a fun character, he was dark and mysterious and yet you know you can trust him. I thought he and Kayla had great chemistry together. <br /><br />The book is fast paced with a lot going on. There were some twists and although some things were resolved a little too quickly I really enjoyed the overall story. I loved the setting and Hawthorne’s take on werewolves. If you enjoy werewolf stories I'd recommend giving this one a try. <br /><br /><u>Content</u><br />Romance: Clean<br />Language: Mild, a handful or so (A, B, G, S)<br />Violence: Mild<br />Other: Underage drinking<br /><br />Source: Oyster Unlimited</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17762995818003420596">I was very disappointed when reading Moonlight. Especially the fact that it was like Twilight, just with wolves. At first, I was really excited to read Moonlight! Reading about something new, learning more about wolves, I didn’t notice any “flaw” until reading about a quarter of the book. I started to realize that there were a lot of similarities with Twilight and Moonlight. The concept was the same, the characters were similar, the name of the book, and just the little details is what got me th</span>
  <span id="freeText17762995818003420596" style="display:none">I was very disappointed when reading Moonlight. Especially the fact that it was like Twilight, just with wolves. At first, I was really excited to read Moonlight! Reading about something new, learning more about wolves, I didn’t notice any “flaw” until reading about a quarter of the book. I started to realize that there were a lot of similarities with Twilight and Moonlight. The concept was the same, the characters were similar, the name of the book, and just the little details is what got me the most. (i.e. The Sherpas have matching tattoos on the shoulder.) You can also tell that Moonlight is similar to Twilight because Twilight was published in 2005, while Moonlight was published in 2009. I don’t recommend this book at all, especially if you are a Twilight fan. Though you can always give this a try, just don’t be surprised if your disappointed. After forcing myself to finish Moonlight, I didn’t bother to pick up the next book, Full Moon. Hopefully the next book I read about vampires or wolves won’t be like this one.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://teenagereader.com/moonlight-by-rachel-hawthorne/">http://teenagereader.com/moonlight-by...</a></span>

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1553214595" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7956697634733521375"><b>3/5 STARS</b><br/><br/>An incredibly entertaining and devourable 3 Star read.<br/><br/><br/>I read this book back in my Twilight days when I was high off the binge of the quartet. I only read this first installment within this series and for years I never knew what the book was called or if my memory of it was a fever dream. <br/><br/>A couple years back I rediscovered it in a Half Price Books and it was a signed copy! Feeling the Covid19-Reading-Slump take me over, I decided to read it. <br/><br/>I binged it in one sitting. <br/></span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_153104312" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/153104312" />
    <a title="CrystalBookSnob" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2909188-crystalbooksnob"><img alt="CrystalBookSnob" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586277134p2/2909188.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/153104312?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="CrystalBookSnob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="CrystalBookSnob" href="/user/show/2909188-crystalbooksnob">CrystalBookSnob</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer153104312" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15066165970724193898">Moonlight by Rachel Hawthorne was a pretty good read. It was really quick and for the most part held my attention to the end. There were things I liked about the book and things I disliked about it. To be completely honest, I thought the first 125 pages were boring and I was just waiting for the good stuff to happen. I could tell it was boring at first because I left it at a friend’s house and I wasn’t desperate to get it back that second. But I’m glad that I kept reading because it got real exc</span>
  <span id="freeText15066165970724193898" style="display:none">Moonlight by Rachel Hawthorne was a pretty good read. It was really quick and for the most part held my attention to the end. There were things I liked about the book and things I disliked about it. To be completely honest, I thought the first 125 pages were boring and I was just waiting for the good stuff to happen. I could tell it was boring at first because I left it at a friend’s house and I wasn’t desperate to get it back that second. But I’m glad that I kept reading because it got real exciting towards t the end.<br /><br />Hawthorne was not too clear about Kayla’s past before her parents died. Was she a baby when it happened or was she older? How can she just take off for a whole summer and not talk to any of her friends back home? Did she even have any friends? A lot of books start the reader off in the main character’s life when she turns 16 or 17, she has recently moved or sent to live with another relative and the author gives almost no information of their life before the move. It’s their life has just started and they’re making friends for the first time. Moving on.<br /><br />I was totally fooled by the group of “graduate research assistants” who claimed to be studying wolves in the forest. And when Mason forced himself on Kayla, I thought he was for real. I love Kayla and Lucas’s chemistry right from the start. He’s so intense and mysterious and he sounds really hot. Their chemistry only increases when they discover they’re practically soul mates and that he waited his whole life for her and will never love another female the way he loves her. *sigh*<br /><br />The one complaint I have concerns the scene in which she shape shifts for the first time. Before it happened, Lucas described it as this very painful process, comparable to childbirth, in which some people don’t survive. But then Hawthorne only devotes one page to it and the only sensation she describes feeling is her skin tingling. She could have done so much more with this. It could have been this intense bonding experience in which he helps her through one of the most painful events in her life, but it only gets about one page.<br /><br />Overall, I thought it was a pretty good book.<br /><br />I give it a B+</span>
  <a data-text-id="15066165970724193898" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_95829578" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/95829578" />
    <a title="Jen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3471319-jen"><img alt="Jen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1512402337p2/3471319.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/95829578?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen" href="/user/show/3471319-jen">Jen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">those with a sweet tooth.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3471319-jen?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3471319-jen?shelf=bought-at-half-price-books">bought-at-half-price-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer95829578" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12046097617533755851">Reading this book was like opening a box of varying chocolates and, even with the all-encompassing fear that you'll choose one with the stale nuts or unexplained goo, biting into one of those deliciously sweet caramel-wielding candies on your first try.<br/><br/>Moonlight was exactly what I was looking for: sweet, decadent, fluffy. <br/><br/>Let me share a disclaimer that this book was in no way ground-breaking, nor did it venture into unchartered territory. I didn't go in with high-expectations, but one of my favo</span>
  <span id="freeText12046097617533755851" style="display:none">Reading this book was like opening a box of varying chocolates and, even with the all-encompassing fear that you'll choose one with the stale nuts or unexplained goo, biting into one of those deliciously sweet caramel-wielding candies on your first try.<br /><br />Moonlight was exactly what I was looking for: sweet, decadent, fluffy. <br /><br />Let me share a disclaimer that this book was in no way ground-breaking, nor did it venture into unchartered territory. I didn't go in with high-expectations, but one of my favorite book bloggers held this series in high regard, so I read it anyway. <br /><br />Kayla, the newbie sherpa, wasn't too boring and her love interest, Lucas, was pretty yummy (except the silver, black, brown, and white hair. I couldn't help but picture a freaking calico cat whenever I read about his hair color. They may be cute, but sexy, they are not.) I also liked the different dynamics that her friends Lindsey and (especially!) snarky Brittany. Hawthorne drops subtle hints about the respective stories of the other sherpas and their backgrounds, and it made me want more. <br /><br />I like the whole archaic idea of a male guardian choosing his destined lover and, if she refuses him, he walks through life alone. It would be terrible if this was the real world, but it's fiction and it raises the stakes and adds an element of "will she or won't she?" when it comes to his chosen mate making her decision to accept him. Reading the prologue, I thought Kayla would have more of a conflict in taking Lucas as her soulmate, but actually the conflict was more about her accepting that she was a shifter. <br /><br />This short and quick read had an L.J. Smith's Nightworld feel to it. Everything's predictable, flufftastic, and it takes half the book for the heroine to find out she's EXTRASPECIAL... but it totally works. I did not once get bored with this cute little book. <br /><br />A definite guilty pleasure read, but a good one. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12046097617533755851" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('jEtJJsUmTTTDi28/xc/rzMOE/glt/Ef3pGZpk+aPf93q1eSV/eRf4Lc6aNhSfRwOEaEyICnESxcA6Gajh6o68A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ineGNi5OTgoLK/Q4vh6srE+DmGH11ZGoyfBW46sKzl/s6SuFFoxc3n+a898prFtunaZUSLHtnUhtflnTyi+Lcg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7936454535967785116">aka <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/275067.Jade_Parker?bf=500&from_search=true' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jade Parker</a> and also writes with her son as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6162355.J_A_London?bf=500&from_search=true' rel='nofollow noopener'>J.A. London</a> <br/>(also writes romance under <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/104926.Lorraine_Heath' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lorraine Heath</a>)<br/><br/>Rachel Hawthorne, who also writes as Lorraine Heath and Jade Parker, is the daughter of a British beauty (her mother won second place in a beauty contest sponsored by Max Factor® during which she received a kiss from Caesar Romero-who played the Joker on the old Batman TV series) and a Texan who w</span>
  <span id="freeText7936454535967785116" style="display:none">aka <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/275067.Jade_Parker?bf=500&amp;from_search=true" rel="nofollow noopener">Jade Parker</a> and also writes with her son as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6162355.J_A_London?bf=500&amp;from_search=true" rel="nofollow noopener">J.A. London</a> <br />(also writes romance under <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/104926.Lorraine_Heath" rel="nofollow noopener">Lorraine Heath</a>)<br /><br />Rachel Hawthorne, who also writes as Lorraine Heath and Jade Parker, is the daughter of a British beauty (her mother won second place in a beauty contest sponsored by Max Factor® during which she received a kiss from Caesar Romero-who played the Joker on the old Batman TV series) and a Texan who was stationed at Bovingdon while serving in the air force. Lorraine was born in Watford, Herts, England, but soon after moved to Texas. Her "dual" nationality has given her a love for all things British and Texan. She enjoys weaving both heritages through her stories.<br /><br />When she received her BA degree in psychology from the University of Texas, she had no idea she had gained a foundation that would help her to create believable characters—characters that are often described as “real people.” She writes for both adult and young adult readers. She received a Romantic Times Career Achievement Award for Americana historicals. Her novels have been recognized with a RITA, Romance Writers of America’s most prestigious award for excellence, a HOLT medallion award honoring outstanding literary fiction, a Romantic Times Reviewer’s Choice Award, five Texas Gold Awards, the Golden Quill Award, the Rising Star Award as well as other awards and recognitions. Her novels have been selections of the Doubleday and Rhapsody Book Club. Her novels have appeared on bestseller lists, including USA Today, Waldenbooks, and most recently, the New York Times.</span>
